#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	A statistical analysis of the effects of urease pre-treatment on the
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	of the urinary metabolome by gas chromatographymass spectrometry
ST:STUDY_TYPE                    	Analytical Comparison
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Urease pre-treatment of urine has been utilized since the early 1960s to remove
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	levels of urea from samples prior to further processing and analysis by gas
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	spectrometry (GCMS). Aside from the obvious depletion or elimination of urea,
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	effect, if any, of urease pre-treatment on the urinary metabolome has not been
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	in detail. Here, we report the results of three separate but related
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	that were designed to assess possible indirect effects of urease pre-treatment
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	the urinary metabolome as measured by GCMS. In total, 235 GCMS analyses
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	performed and over 106 identified and 200 unidentified metabolites were
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	across the three experiments. The results showed that data from urease
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	samples (1) had the same or lower coefficients of variance among reproducibly
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	metabolites, (2) more accurately reflected quantitative differences and the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	ratios among different urine volumes, and (3) increased the number of
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	identifications. Overall, we observed no negative consequences of urease
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	In contrast, urease pre-treatment enhanced the ability to distinguish between
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	and biological sample types compared to no treatment. Taken together, these
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	show that urease pre-treatment of urine offers multiple beneficial effects that
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	any artifacts that may be introduced to the data in urinary metabolomics
ST:INSTITUTE                     	Pacific Northwest National Laboratory
ST:DEPARTMENT                    	Biological Separation and Mass Spectrometry
ST:LAST_NAME                     	Metz
ST:FIRST_NAME                    	Thomas
ST:ADDRESS                       	-
ST:EMAIL                         	thomas.metz@pnnl.gov
ST:PHONE                         	-
ST:NUM_GROUPS                    	6
ST:TOTAL_SUBJECTS                	235

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	Approval for the conduct of this programmatic research was obtained from the
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	Northwest National Laboratory Institutional Review Board. Urine samples from
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	male and female donors (n = 20 each, Supplemental Table S1) after an overnight
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	were purchased from Bioreclamation, LLC (Hicksville, NY) and received frozen on
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	ice and deidentified. To create a uniform sample for Experiments 1 and 2 (see
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	aliquots from each individual sample were pooled, realiquoted, and stored at
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	until used.
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Urine
CO:STORAGE_CONDITIONS            	-80° C
#TREATMENT
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	Varying Volume with Urease / Male vs. Female with Urease / Constant Volume with
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	/ Constant Volume with 100 µL Water
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	To evaluate whether the effects of urease pre-treatment of urine varied with
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	volume of urine prepared, we compared the urine metabolite profiles from pooled
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	after pre-treatment with urease (UT) and after no treatment (NT) using various
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	of urine. For this, several volumes (5, 10, 25, 50, and 100 µL) of the pooled
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	sample were incubated (n = 3, each) with 100 µL of a 1 mg/mL solution of
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	or were not subjected to any treatment. / Finally, to evaluate whether any
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	introduced by urease pre-treatment on the urinary metabolome interfered with
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	ability to distinguish between comparative samples, we compared the metabolite
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	from individual male and female urine samples after pre-treatment with urease
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	after no treatment (previous metabolomics studies of male and female urines
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	et al., 2008; Slupsky et al., 2007; Saude et al., 2007; Psihogios et al., 2008)
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	reported differences in metabolite levels). For this, 50 µL aliquots of
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	male and female urine samples (n = 20, each) were blocked, randomized, and then
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	with 50 µL of a 1 mg/mL solution of urease (UT) or were not subjected to any
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	(NT), each as described above. / To initially evaluate the effects of urease
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	on the urinary metabolome, we compared the urine metabolite profiles from
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	urine after pre-treatment with urease, water, or no treatment at all. For this,
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	uL aliquots of the pooled urine sample were incubated (n = 5, each) with 100 uL
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	a 1 mg/mL solution of urease (Sigma-Aldrich catalog number U4002) prepared in
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	(urease-treated; UT) or an equal volume of water alone (water-treated;
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	for 30 min at 37 C with mild shaking (500 rpm). Identical aliquots (n = 5) were
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	subjected to any treatment (no treatment; NT) and allowed to sit at room
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	for 30 min. / To initially evaluate the effects of urease pre-treatment on the
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	metabolome, we compared the urine metabolite profiles from pooled urine after
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	with urease, water, or no treatment at all. For this, 100 uL aliquots of the
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	urine sample were incubated (n = 5, each) with 100 uL of a 1 mg/mL solution of
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	(Sigma-Aldrich catalog number U4002) prepared in water (urease-treated; UT)
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	an equal volume of water alone (water-treated; WT) for 30 min at 37 C with
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	shaking (500 rpm). Identical aliquots (n = 5) were not subjected to any
TR:TREATMENT_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS   	(no treatment; NT) and allowed to sit at room temperature for 30 min.
TR:TREATMENT                     	Abiotic
TR:TREATMENT_COMPOUND            	Urease / Urease / Urease / Water
TR:TREATMENT_DOSE                	1 mg/ml / 1 mg/ml / 1 mg/ml / --
TR:TREATMENT_DOSEVOLUME          	100 µL / 50 µL / 100 µL / 100 µL
TR:HUMAN_FASTING                 	Overnight Fast
#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	concomitant protein precipitation with cold methanol, vortexing,
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	supernatent dried in vacuo, stored at -80° c, chemical derivitization
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	Metabolites were extracted with concomitant protein precipitation by addition
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	1 mL of cold (-20 C) methanol with vortexing for 30 s, and precipitated
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	were removed by centrifugation at 15,000xg for 10 min at 4 C. The supernatants
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	transferred to glass autosampler vials and then dried in vacuo prior to
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	derivatization. If the extracts could not be immediately derivatized an d
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	by GCMS, then they were stored at -80C. Dried metabolite extracts were
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	derivatized using a modified version of the protocol used to create FiehnLib
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	et al., 2009). Briefly, dried metabolite extracts were dried again to remove
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	residual water if they had been stored at -80°C. To protect carbonyl groups
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	reduce the number of tautomeric isomers, 20 µL of methoxyamine in pyridine (30
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	were added to each sample, followed by vortexing for 30 s and incubation at
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	with generous shaking (1000 rpm) for 90 min. At this point, the sample vials
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	inverted one time to capture any condensation of solvent at the cap surface,
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	by a brief centrifugation at 1000×g for 1 min. To derivatize hydroxyl and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	groups to trimethylsilyated (TMS) forms, 80 µL of
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	(MSTFA) with 1% trimethylchlorosilane (TMCS) were then added to each vial,
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	by vortexing for 10 s and incubation at 37°C with shaking (1000 rpm) for 30
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	Again, the sample vials were inverted one time, followed by centrifugation at
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	for 5 min. The samples were allowed to cool to room temperature and were
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_COMMENTS  	in the same day.
SP:PROCESSING_METHOD             	precipitation, centrifugation
SP:PROCESSING_STORAGE_CONDITIONS 	dried in vacuo, stored at -80° C
SP:EXTRACTION_METHOD             	concomitant protein precipitation by addition of 1 mL of cold (-20 C) methanol
SP:EXTRACTION_METHOD             	vortexing and centrifugation
SP:EXTRACT_ENRICHMENT            	dried in vacuo
SP:EXTRACT_STORAGE               	-80° C
SP:SAMPLE_RESUSPENSION           	20 µL of methoxyamine in pyridine (30 mg/mL)
SP:SAMPLE_DERIVATIZATION         	20 µL of methoxyamine in pyridine (30 mg/mL), 80 µL of
SP:SAMPLE_DERIVATIZATION         	(MSTFA) with 1% trimethylchlorosilane (TMCS)
#CHROMATOGRAPHY
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	Agilent 7890A gas chromatograph with a HP-5MS gas chromatography column using
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_TYPE           	-
CH:INSTRUMENT_NAME               	Agilent 7890A
CH:COLUMN_NAME                   	HP-5MS (30 m x 0.25 mm x 0.25 m film thickness)
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	Chromatography was carried out on an Agilent 7890A gas chromatograph using the
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	software (Chemstation) and a HP-5MS gas chromatography column (Agilent
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	Santa Clara, CA; 30 m x 0.25 mm x 0.25 m film thickness). The sample injection
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	was splitless, and 1 L of each sample was injected. The injection port
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	was held at 250 C throughout the analysis. The GC oven was held at 60 C for 1
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	after injection, and the temperature was then increased to 325 C by 10 C/min,
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	by a 5 min hold at 325 C. The helium gas flow rates for each Experiment were
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	by the Agilent Retention Time Locking function based on analysis of deuterated
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_COMMENTS       	acid and were in the range of 0.450.5 mL/min.
CH:FLOW_RATE                     	0.450.5 mL/min
CH:INJECTION_TEMPERATURE         	250 C
CH:SAMPLE_INJECTION              	1 L, splitless
CH:ANALYTICAL_TIME               	37.5 min
CH:OVEN_TEMPERATURE              	60 C for 1 min, then increased to 325 C by 10 C/min, followed by a 5 min hold
CH:OVEN_TEMPERATURE              	325 C
CH:SAMPLE_SYRINGE_SIZE           	10 L
#ANALYSIS
AN:ANALYSIS_TYPE                 	MS
AN:LABORATORY_NAME               	Biological Separations & Mass Spectrometry group, Pacific Northwest National
AN:LABORATORY_NAME               	(www.omics.pnl.gov)
AN:ACQUISITION_DATE              	2013
AN:SOFTWARE_VERSION              	Metabolite Detector vs. 2.0.6 beta
AN:DATA_FORMAT                   	Raw .D.Zip; Processed .CDF
#MS
MS:INSTRUMENT_NAME               	Agilent 7890A GC / 5975C MS
MS:INSTRUMENT_TYPE               	Single quadrupole
MS:MS_TYPE                       	EI
MS:ION_MODE                      	POSITIVE
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	An Agilent GC 7890A coupled with a single quadrupole MSD 5975C (Agilent
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Inc.; Santa Clara, CA, USA) was used, and the samples were blocked and analyzed
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	random order for each experiment. Data were collected over the mass range
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	m/z. A mixture of FAMEs (C8-C28) was analyzed once per day together with the
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	for retention index alignment purposes during subsequent data analysis.
MS:SCAN_RANGE_MOVERZ             	50-550 m/z
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	GCMS raw data files from each Experiment were processed using the Metabolite
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	software, version 2.0.6 beta. Briefly, Agilent.D files were converted to netCDF
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	using Agilent Chemstation, followed by conversion to binary files using
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Detector. Retention indices of detected metabolites were calculated based on
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	analysis of the FAMEs mixture, followed by their chromatographic alignment
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	all analyses after deconvolution. Metabolites were initially identified by
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	experimental spectra to an augmented version of FiehnLib (i.e., the Agilent
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Metabolomics Retention Time Locked (RTL) Library, containing spectra and
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	retention indices for over 700 metabolites), using a Metabolite Detector match
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	threshold of 0.6 (combined retention index and spectral probability). All
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	identifications were manually validated to reduce deconvolution errors during
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	data-processing and to eliminate false identifications. The NIST 08 GCMS
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	was also used to cross validate the spectral matching scores obtained using the
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	library and to provide identifications of unmatched metabolites. The three most
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	fragment ions in the spectra of each identified metabolite were automatically
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	by Metabolite Detector, and their summed abundances were integrated across the
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	elution profile; fragment ions due to trimethylsilylation (i.e. m/z 73 and 147)
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	excluded from the determination of metabolite abundance. A matrix of identified
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	unidentified metabolite features (characterized by mass spectra and retention
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	and assigned as unknown), and their abundances was created for each
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	for statistical analysis. Features resulting from GC column bleeding were
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	from the data matrices prior to further data processing and analysis.
